Source Code

This source code is very close to the Apollo Guidance Computer software for the Apollo 13 Lunar module. This revision of the Luminary 131 program is from December of 1969, whereas there was a later revision in January of 1970, and still another revision in February, which is the code that flew on the mission. As far as this transcription is concerned, it was originally from a copy made in 1991 of a printout from the collection of AGC developer Don Eyles for collector David Craig. It was subsequently scanned by Gary Neff, reprocessed for online presentation at the now-discontinued History of Recent Science and Technology (HRST) website of MIT's Dibner Institute (the full-quality scans being discarded in the process), and finally transcribed by Ron Burkey for the Virtual AGC Project. Although a high-quality replacement scan for a completely illegible page was later provided by Gary Neff, the reduced legibility of the reprocessed HRST posting nevertheless caused many errors to be introduced into the transcription. Accordingly, a second scan of the same physical printout was made in 2017 for the Virtual AGC Project's collection at the Internet Archive, and used to correct the transcription errors. All of the scanned materials mentioned, as well as other Luminary 131 related material, are available online. Don Eyles apprently made additional hand-written notes in printout between 1991 and 2017, so the two scans are not identical in that respect. The page-headings in the printout read, in part:
	GAP:  ASSEMBLE REVISION 131 OF AGC PROGRAM LUMINARY BY NASA 2021112-091
	17:53 DEC. 19, 1969
Note that the date is the date the printout was made, not the date on which the program revision was released, although these happen to be very close together. 

000002,000002:                                                                                                  #  Copyright:    Public domain.
000003,000003:                                                                                                  #  Filename:     MAIN.agc
000004,000004:                                                                                                  #  Purpose:      The main source file for Luminary 1C, revision 131.
000005,000005:                                                                                                  #                It is part of the source code for the Lunar Module's (LM)
000006,000006:                                                                                                  #                Apollo Guidance Computer (AGC) for Apollo 13.
000007,000007:                                                                                                  #  Assembler:    yaYUL
000008,000008:                                                                                                  #  Contact:      Ron Burkey <info@sandroid.org>.
000009,000009:                                                                                                  #  Website:      www.ibiblio.org/apollo/index.html
000010,000010:                                                                                                  #  Mod history:  04/12/03 RSB.   Began.
000011,000011:                                                                                                  #                05/05/03 RSB.   ...continued.
000012,000012:                                                                                                  #                05/11/03 RSB    Draft of this file completed.
000013,000013:                                                                                                  #                06/08/03 RSB    Drafts of all the included files completed.
000014,000014:                                                                                                  #                05/14/05 RSB    Corrected website reference above.
000015,000015:                                                                                                  #                06/30/09 RSB    Added an experimental HTML note.
000016,000016:                                                                                                  #                2017-01-06 RSB  Changed page-number references so that they
000017,000017:                                                                                                  #                                refer to the markings on the physical pages
000018,000018:                                                                                                  #                                of the printout (rather than PDF "pages" in
000019,000019:                                                                                                  #                                the file 1729.pdf, which is no longer the
000020,000020:                                                                                                  #                                associated reference material).
000021,000021:                                                                                                  #                2017-01-20 RSB  Changed GOTOP00H to GOTOPOOH in all *.agc
000022,000022:                                                                                                  #                                files.  There are probably more POO problems
000023,000023:                                                                                                  #                                but those are the only ones I fixed.
000024,000024:                                                                                                  #                2017-02-12 RSB  References to the scanned assembly listing
000025,000025:                                                                                                  #                                have been updated now that a more-legible
000026,000026:                                                                                                  #                                scan is available than before.
000027,000027: 
000028,000028:                                                                                                  #  The contents of these "Luminary131" files were originally (2003)
000029,000029:                                                                                                  #  transcribed from a scanned document obtained from MIT's
000030,000030:                                                                                                  #  now-defunct history or recent technology website, but which can be
000031,000031:                                                                                                  #  consulted now at
000032,000032:                                                                                                  #        http://www.ibiblio.org/apollo/ScansForConversion/Luminary131
000033,000033:                                                                                                  #  As of 2017, however, there is a far-more legible scan, created from the same
000034,000034:                                                                                                  #  physical printout, which you should instead consult, at either
000035,000035:                                                                                                  #        http://www.ibiblio.org/apollo/ScansForConversion/Luminary131-Eyles
000036,000036:                                                                                                  #  or
000037,000037:                                                                                                  #        https://archive.org/details/luminary131agcpr00miti
000038,000038:                                                                                                  #  Notations within the original program listing read, in part:
000039,000039: 
000040,000040:                                                                                                  #        NASA Apollo LUMINARY 131 (1C) Program Source Code Listing.
000041,000041:                                                                                                  #        MIT Instrumentation/Draper Laboratory -- 19 December 1969, 1742 pages.
000042,000042:                                                                                                  #        This listing contains the flight program for the Lunar Module 
000043,000043:                                                                                                  #        as created by MIT's Draper Lab for the Apollo 13/14 moon missions.
000044,000044: 
000045,000045:                                                                                                  #  This file is a little different from the other Luminary131 files I'm providing, 
000046,000046:                                                                                                  #  in that it doesn't represent anything that appears directly in the original source.  
000047,000047:                                                                                                  #  What I (RSB) have done for organizational purposes is to split the huge monolithic
000048,000048:                                                                                                  #  source code into smaller, more manageable chunks--i.e., into individual source 
000049,000049:                                                                                                  #  files.  Those files are rejoined within this file as "includes".  It just makes
000050,000050:                                                                                                  #  it a little easier to work with.  The code chunks correspond to natural divisions
000051,000051:                                                                                                  #  into sub-programs.  In fact, these divisions are more-or-less specified by
000052,000052:                                                                                                  #  the source code itself.  Refer to the "TABLE OF SUBROUTINE LOG SECTIONS" at the
000053,000053:                                                                                                  #  very beginning of the file ASSEMBLY_AND_OPERATION_INFORMATION.agc.
000054,000054: 
000055,000055:                                                                                                  #  It may be reasonably asked why tens of thousands of lines of source are joined by
000056,000056:                                                                                                  #  means of inclusion, rather than simply assembling the source files individually and
000057,000057:                                                                                                  #  then linking them to form the executable.  The answer is that the original 
000058,000058:                                                                                                  #  development team had no linker.  The builds were monolithic just like this.
000059,000059:                                                                                                  #  There was a big emphasis on reusability of the code in the original project, 
000060,000060:                                                                                                  #  apparently, but this reusability took the form of inserting your deck of 
000061,000061:                                                                                                  #  punch-cards at the appropriate position in somebody else's deck of punch-cards.
000062,000062:                                                                                                  #  So, indeed, the method of file-inclusion is a very fair representation of the 
000063,000063:                                                                                                  #  methods used in the original development ... with the improvement, of course,
000064,000064:                                                                                                  #  that you no longer have to worry about dropping the card deck.  On the other hand, 
000065,000065:                                                                                                  #  I wasn't there at the time, so I may have no idea what I'm talking about.
000066,000066: 
000067,000067:                                                                                                  #  Finally, note that the original Apollo AGC assembler (called "YUL") is no longer 
000068,000068:                                                                                                  #  available (as far as I can tell).  The replacement assembler yaYUL accepts 
000069,000069:                                                                                                  #  a slightly different format for the source code from what YUL accepted, so the 
000070,000070:                                                                                                  #  source code has been targeted for assembly with yaYUL.
000071,000071: 
000072,000072:                                                                                                  #  What follows is simply a bunch of file-includes for the individual code chunks.
000073,000073:                                                                                                  #  I've marked the page numbers vs. the original scanned listing (1729.pdf) to 
000074,000074:                                                                                                  #  make proof-reading easier.  Besides, the scanned listing contains a lot of
000075,000075:                                                                                                  #  interesting tables (cross-referenced to page numbers) created by YUL, 
000076,000076:                                                                                                  #  but not duplicated by yaYUL, so it's still valuable even if the source-files
000077,000077:                                                                                                  #  listed below are in hand.  Notice, though, that the page number herein are those
000078,000078:                                                                                                  #  the scanned (PDF) file, and not those which are marked on the scanned pages
000079,000079:                                                                                                  #  themselves, so there is not an exact correspondence between YUL-generated
000080,000080:                                                                                                  #  page numbers appearing within tables and the page numbers marked in this source
000081,000081:                                                                                                  #  code.
000082,000082:
